<div id="review_199599128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199599128" />
    <a title="jD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2415283-jd"><img alt="jD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283353615p2/2415283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199599128?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jD" href="/user/show/2415283-jd">jD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=fantasy_urban">fantasy_urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=2_kindle_own">2_kindle_own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=magic_witches">magic_witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199599128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer268333696559943201">After reading this installment, I better understood why some fans weren't feeling it. I am not one of those. I believe my positive experience with the book is because I didn't have to wait and generous spoilers. In truth, spoilers only tell me what happened but not how I will feel about it. <br/><br/>I did not expect to get excited about Pierce. I thought I would be unhappy that Trent is hardly in the book. I thought it was time for the gorgoyle to state his business. I thought Marshall was going to turn </span>
  <span id="freeText268333696559943201" style="display:none">After reading this installment, I better understood why some fans weren't feeling it. I am not one of those. I believe my positive experience with the book is because I didn't have to wait and generous spoilers. In truth, spoilers only tell me what happened but not how I will feel about it. <br /><br />I did not expect to get excited about Pierce. I thought I would be unhappy that Trent is hardly in the book. I thought it was time for the gorgoyle to state his business. I thought Marshall was going to turn out like Nick and screw Rachael over. I thought Ivy would fall back to her old ways. So now I trust spoilers less as the result of my own experience.<br /><br />Most of what I wanted the plot to do was satisfy my emotional fix. Had I waited a year for the book with another year or two wait for the next one, I would have been harsh. I have the luxury of picking up the next installment and the one after that at the library. I just love when I find a series that's mostly published or finished.<br /><br />As with the previous book, Rachael needed to do some literal and figurative attic cleaning. She needed to find a balance with her magic, family, friends, and enemies. I believe the old Rachael was not ready for the things Ms. Harrison will throw her way in upcoming books. Now she has a past full of regrets and lessons that she can pull from to temper her charcter in a pinch. I never liked the fact that Rachael does not have a killer instinct but that also separates her quite a bit from many other heroines out there. She has plenty of killers around her so death will follow whether by her hands or not, so I work with that. The boyfriend thing is not as troublesome as before. Nick will never worm his way back in her heart, Kristen is gone, Marshall headed for the hills, and Pierce is a ghost. I like Pierce as a distraction/placeholder until the 'magic moment' with Trent. Yes, I am still in camp Trent. Rachael's constant thoughts about how hot he is can't just be for nothing. She doesn't react that way to anyone else.<br /><br />I am glad this book got rid of some nasties that had run their course. Kristen is put to rest as he deserved. Some may have felt cheated but I loved that Kristen was his own hero in the end.<br /><br />I am looking forward to reading the next one. I have a couple of books I need to read beforehand for my book club but damn Rachael, I'm gonna miss you for a few weeks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="268333696559943201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205709185" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205709185?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theshrewedshrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theshrewedshrew" href="/user/show/5865861-theshrewedshrew">Theshrewedshrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5865861-theshrewedshrew?shelf=the-hollows">the-hollows</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205709185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6005342418291150379">One of the last lines of the book defines the entire book for me. <br/><br/>Al says something along the lines of "But he is Rachel candy..." I can't remember now if it was a statement or a question, but assuredly it is hilarious. Its one of the few lines and reason I still read The Hollows... <br/>yeah I know if your 7 books in you should already have a reason, but Rachel is one of the most whiny rhymes with witchy character. <br/><br/>She has this moral code, which makes noooo sense. They are on the boat, people are as</span>
  <span id="freeText6005342418291150379" style="display:none">One of the last lines of the book defines the entire book for me. <br /><br />Al says something along the lines of "But he is Rachel candy..." I can't remember now if it was a statement or a question, but assuredly it is hilarious. Its one of the few lines and reason I still read The Hollows... <br />yeah I know if your 7 books in you should already have a reason, but Rachel is one of the most whiny rhymes with witchy character. <br /><br />She has this moral code, which makes noooo sense. They are on the boat, people are asleep... She knows the bomb is going to go off, and Trent is able to feed her line energy... <br /><br />So what does she do, <br /><br />A. Grab all the people and try and hold a huge circle, with as many survivors as possible? <br />B. Cry and moan.<br />C. Do absolutely nothing for them and blame everyone else?<br /><br />Ding ding ding...<br /><br />So next we have Rachel Morgan in an easy to win situation... She is shunned, she is attacked by a clearly identifiable person, and what does she do? Signs a piece of paper saying she did it. HURRAY!!<br /><br />Rachel Morgan is dense, she can't afford her rent currently, can't do much, whines about Al, but wants to get more proficent with Lay Lines as seen in the last book where she tried to pay for school... So does she <br /><br />A. Take a 5000 year old master of Magic up on his offer to tutor her.<br />B. Sit at home in P.J.'s crying over the fact she is shunned, instead of taking the oranges and making OJ?<br /><br />Yeah... Rachel Morgan... Master of the thick head, and then she some how manages to make vast jumps at things like storing energy, but what good does that ever do her, if she doesn't have a stored curse.<br /><br />She is often one of the few people who I agree with, in most Urban fantasy books, magic users rarely expect the head on fist rush.<br /><br /><br />I get the effectiveness of that coupled with the sleep charms, however... after the initial shock is over, anyone left standing rules over Morgan, and its sad to see her be shocked into ineffectiveness the second that happens... again... and again... and probably again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6005342418291150379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_920182369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920182369" />
    <a title="T.J. Day" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7632433-t-j-day"><img alt="T.J. Day" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573337275p2/7632433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920182369?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.J. Day" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.J. Day" href="/user/show/7632433-t-j-day">T.J. Day</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061138027" href="/book/show/6344237-white-witch-black-curse">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920182369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3235553566784362092">Banshees! Emotion-sucking monsters with agendas that no man can stand against, White Witch, Black Curse has all kinds of new bad guys. Trent doesn't make much of an appearance in this, mostly because it focuses on the FIB and the novella the book is connected to, "Two Ghosts For Sister Rachel." When Glenn is injured, things are made personal and although Rachel doesn't want to go face to face with an aura-damaging banshee, she knows she doesn't have much of a choice.<br/><br/>A lot of things happen in thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3235553566784362092" style="display:none">Banshees! Emotion-sucking monsters with agendas that no man can stand against, White Witch, Black Curse has all kinds of new bad guys. Trent doesn't make much of an appearance in this, mostly because it focuses on the FIB and the novella the book is connected to, "Two Ghosts For Sister Rachel." When Glenn is injured, things are made personal and although Rachel doesn't want to go face to face with an aura-damaging banshee, she knows she doesn't have much of a choice.<br /><br />A lot of things happen in this book, with the meeting of somewhat new characters Mia and Pierce, the usual trouble from Al, the bonding between Ivy and Rachel gets stronger yet again, and the fallout of Rachel in the witch community, including with Marshal, and we discover who killed her lover. Not to mention, the author is also really setting up for A Perfect Blood with the introduction of the doctor in this. Sometimes it's amazing how much gets thrown at the poor girl. <br /><br />For me though, this story was driven by the plot over the character. As much as I like Rachel's troublesome personality, she kind of bugged me in this always thinking she was going to get her friends killed and that she was some albatross. I hate that she blames herself for all the trouble. Sometimes shit just happens and I'm glad her character comes to realize that in the next couple books. <br /><br />I've never really been a fan of the whole "you need to read the novella to understand what goes on in the story" thing. I'm sure that doing enovellas and anthologies is great for the author and publishers money wise, and even though I've read them doesn't mean everyone else has, and you miss so much just by not reading it. Pierce is introduced in the holiday story and Mia has her own story in the Hotter Than Hell. Though the story is understandable enough, as a first-time reader way back when, I found myself struggling to put things together because I was missing so much. So I guess that would be my only complaint. <br /><br />Onto the next one, which I am over halfway through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3235553566784362092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62477069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62477069" />
    <a title="Natasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2496802-natasha"><img alt="Natasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572201679p2/2496802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62477069?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha" href="/user/show/2496802-natasha">Natasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62477069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6733206578887859456">I've been a fan of Kim Harrison since I first read DEAD WITCH WALKING and I've never been disappointed. She writes the stories you wish you could have and makes you emotionally attached throughout. I don't think I could choose a favorite from this series but this installment is near the top.<br/>It's action packed and a fast paced read. I read it in a few hours and could not put it down. <br/> In this installment she puts to rest some ghosts and fights a lot of bad guys. She really goes though a lot of to</span>
  <span id="freeText6733206578887859456" style="display:none">I've been a fan of Kim Harrison since I first read DEAD WITCH WALKING and I've never been disappointed. She writes the stories you wish you could have and makes you emotionally attached throughout. I don't think I could choose a favorite from this series but this installment is near the top.<br />It's action packed and a fast paced read. I read it in a few hours and could not put it down. <br /> In this installment she puts to rest some ghosts and fights a lot of bad guys. She really goes though a lot of tolls, both emotionally and physically in this book and I felt really attached to her character. <br /> There is also a great short story featuring Jenks and Bis in the Anthology Unbound that really gives you that Hollows addiction a kick until the next book. I cannot wait to read BLACK MAGIC SANCTION in 2010, her books never disappoints! <br /> The Hollows is a Urban Fantasy series must! </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8m8tfvaUukESL4uA3yIucia76VjyvQPIV/zLEHsB1IbISUSsTcpzKbUEP+Eo1ySt8OQOkDwwja8Mgo2htkImHA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2CBk6udwQXkF6rmU0/3958nxj6D7ML1d4f6QlqyRVlbiBg04XC6IEaLBDfUkCPc4H65oaDW9Mzq6gNYnYdKkzA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText10731439985511804160" style="display:none">Kim Harrison is best known as the author of the New York Times #1 best selling Hollows series, but she has written more than urban fantasy and has published over two-dozen books spanning the gamut from young adult, thriller, several anthologies, and has scripted two original graphic novels. She has also published traditional fantasy under the name Dawn Cook. Kim is currently working on a new Hollows book between other, non related, urban fantasy projects.<br />Kim reaches out to her audience at Facebook <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/KimHarrisonsHollows?ref=ts">https://www.facebook.com/KimHarrisons...</a> <br />Instagram<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/kim_harrison_author/">https://instagram.com/kim_harrison_au...</a><br />and her blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kimharrison.wordpress.com/">http://kimharrison.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><b>other pseudonyms:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/64216.Dawn_Cook" rel="nofollow noopener">Dawn Cook</a></span>
